National Middle and High School Students' Anti-Drug Essay Contest Deadline 222

Over a Thousand Essays Received from Middle and High School Groups

Evaluators Hired to Begin Grading Immediately

The National Student Anti-Drug Essay Contest, sponsored by the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association, closed its registration on the 15th of last month. Yesterday was the deadline for submissions. Participation from middle and high schools across the country was quite enthusiastic. Evaluation committee members have now been hired and will begin grading immediately. Details are as follows:

Deadline for Submissions: Yesterday marked the deadline for submissions. Over sixty universities participated, submitting over a hundred essays in the university group. Over four hundred middle schools participated, submitting over nine hundred essays in the middle school group, totaling over a thousand essays. Participating schools were widespread. Universities participating included Peking University, Tsinghua University, Shandong Qilu University, Sichuan University, Guangdong National University, Wuhan University, Nanjing Central University, Zhejiang Zhijiang University, and local universities such as Jinan, Shanghai, Guanghua, and Political Science schools, all of which had student participation.

Essay Content: The essay topic for the university group was "The Current Situation of the Opium Scourge in This Locality and Effective Eradication Plans," describing the production, sale, taxation, transportation, and consumption of opium in various regions, as well as the impact of opium on society, economy, morality, and law. The essay topic for the middle school group was "The Fate of Opium Addicts," describing personal experiences with opium addicts, including their backgrounds, families, the reasons for their addiction, and the various negative consequences they suffer after becoming addicted.

Grading Begins: The association has hired Jiang Wenyu, He De, Li Ting'an, Wang Jingqi, Wang Yunwu, and Wang Yazheng as evaluation committee members for the university group, and Zhu Lide, Meng Shouchun, Wang Changbao, Shen Junru, Xie Chunmu, and Wu Youfen as evaluation committee members for the middle school group. They will begin grading separately immediately.

Evaluation Criteria: The evaluation criteria are based on the following points, with scores assigned accordingly: A. Accuracy of factual investigation accounts for 40%; B. Coherence of thought structure accounts for 30%; C. Conciseness and incisiveness of written narration accounts for 30%.

Results Announced Next Spring: Due to the large number of essays received, grading will be time-consuming and the results will not be announced until next spring. Ten winners will be selected in the university group and thirty winners in the middle school group. In addition to awarding medals and certificates to the winners, the association will award scholarships to the first, second, and third-place winners in the university group, and the first, second, third, fourth, and fifth-place winners in the middle school group, with varying amounts. The distribution of funds will be based on the amount of prize money raised.

Therefore, the content is rich, with both illustrations and text. Every issue provides accurate descriptions and explorations of sports theory, administration, training, technology, and teaching materials. The inclusion of dance and games is even more valuable. Hao Gengsheng, a sports inspector from the Ministry of Education, has greatly praised it. Its value can be seen from this. The first issue, the "Inaugural Issue," and the second issue, the "National Games Special Issue," have been reprinted and are about to be sold out. The third issue, the "Primary School Sports Special Issue," has already been published, and the fourth issue is currently being compiled. Recently, subscriptions to the monthly have been coming in one after another, with remittances for subscriptions from as far away as Southeast Asia, Japan, Europe, and the United States. It is popular both domestically and internationally and is truly an honor for domestic periodicals. It is heard that the bookstore, in order to thoroughly promote new sports, still adheres to the principle of sacrifice, with each issue priced at two jiao. Those who subscribe for the whole year within the year can still enjoy a subscription fee of one yuan and two jiao (discounted price until the end of December). Domestic postage is free, and overseas postage is an additional one yuan and eight jiao. However, this is only applicable to direct subscriptions to the bookstore's publishing office and retail department at 554 Fourth Malu. All sports students, sports enthusiasts, and primary and secondary school physical education teachers should definitely subscribe for reference to improve themselves.

Spring and Autumn

Anti-Semitism 248

— Yang Yuesheng

The year 1933 is nearing its end. Among the major events discovered in the world this year, anti-Semitism is undoubtedly one of them.

Japan no longer massacres Koreans, Britain seems much more polite to India, and France has never killed many Annamese. Although they have all lost their countries, their fate is not so bad after all!

The unlucky ones are the overseas Chinese! Driven from the east and expelled from the west, their situation is truly miserable! Next are the Jews!

The Jewish people and the Chinese can be said to be ancient nations of equal standing. The difference is that the Jewish nation was destroyed long ago, while China is still barely surviving!

However, the status of the Chinese in the world seems to be inferior to that of the already extinct Jewish people. The latter has indeed made considerable contributions to the world, and their national unity is also strong, especially their talent for becoming wealthy. These qualities seem to be unmatched by any other nation. If China and the Jewish people were to exchange places, the question of whether the Chinese nation would still exist in the world today would be a real one!

The biggest reason why the German National Socialist government adopted a policy of excluding "Aryan" people and making things difficult for Jews is that they believe the power of the Jews is enough to hinder Germany's survival. In other words, it is nothing more than envy in a broad sense! Of course, the Jews are unwilling to submit to this. The world-renowned German scientist Albert Einstein, therefore, declared his departure from German nationality and became a British subject. They also held national conferences and passed resolutions to boycott German goods and request the League of Nations to sponsor Jewish immigration to Palestine and other places. They also shouted slogans of striving hard and not giving up until death. But the fact remains that Europe does not allow them to establish a foothold. Although we say that we have not tasted the bitterness of national subjugation, the "precedent" of the Jews is not far off, and it should be enough to be alarming!

Since the Jews cannot live in peace in Germany, they are also being squeezed out by the tide of unemployment in Europe. They are unwilling to die just like that, and they are eagerly seeking a livelihood, but where can they go!

So they flood into China like a tide!

China is indeed a good place to go! It is a colony of various powers and a haven for exiles from all countries! Exploitation upon exploitation, parasitism upon parasitism. If someone were to ask me where the Chinese people plan to go in the future? Then this question should also be alarming! Where will we go in the future!

The Nose Expert Who Makes Money with His Nose 249

— Yin Feng

A person with vast wealth but no skills may not be able to eat endlessly forever; a person with a skill but no inheritance may not be forever hungry and cold. A "skill" is a "talent," and with a "talent," one can make money; with money, one can buy food. Those who use their minds earn money by thinking, and thinking is their "talent"; those who use their physical strength earn money by working, and working is their "talent." Whether one uses their mind or physical strength, whether one thinks or works, being able to earn money to make a living is all good.

It can be said that ordinary people in society who earn a living generally cannot escape the scope of using their minds or physical strength. Recently, there was a news story saying that besides using the mind and physical strength, there is now another way to make money: with the nose. In a spice and perfume factory in England, there is a special nose that is worth 20,000 yuan a year. It turns out that there is a chemist in the factory who has special training and research in smell, called the "smell expert." He can get several times more salary than others just by using his nose. So a good nose is very valuable; but its sense of smell must be extremely sharp from the beginning. It can almost discern the situation with just one sniff. It is probably not easy to train to this level.

Mixing various perfumes or blending various spices is an art. In the ingredients of any special perfume that is painstakingly and carefully made, adding even the smallest drop, too much or too little, is enough to ruin everything. In this case, one must consult the "smell expert." His nose takes a sniff and can immediately tell him whether the perfume is mixed correctly or not. If it is not mixed correctly, he can also smell out what should be added. There is also a "smell expert" who makes money with his nose who is hired by a group of old managers of breweries to check the old empty barrels that are sent back to the brewery. He can use his special nose and keen sense of smell to tell which empty barrel is safe to fill with new beer again; and which empty barrel will cause the new beer to spoil if filled again. In addition to checking barrels, the sense of smell also plays an important role in distinguishing the quality of wine.

New York's Kissing Endurance Contest 250

— Zhao Peng

▲ Miss Du Liusi Wins the Championship

▲ Score: Three Hours and Two Minutes

Not long ago, a kissing endurance contest was held in New York City, and many modern men and women, young couples, participated enthusiastically. As a result of the competition, Ms. Du Liusi, after three hours and two minutes of long-term effort, finally won the championship trophy. Ms. Du and her lover have a love history of five years, and they will soon marry her lover. Therefore, this competition won the championship opportunity. After the meeting, someone asked Ms. Du about her thoughts on winning the kissing championship. Ms. Du said: "I have never had the experience of kissing before, and now I have won the kissing championship. It is really unexpected. My sincere love for him can be expressed everywhere. Durable kissing is just a kind of expression of sincere love."

Random Notes on Rural Life 251

— Zi Gao

(1) Rebirth

The rhythm of the machine, the rendering of torches, and snake-like women weave together a picture of urban licentiousness. I passively followed the crowd, drawn into the red vortex. However, mental stimulation, in the aversion to painful memories, made me resolutely run to the countryside.

Having left the pink city, I have been staying in the quiet New Longhua for three months. There, breathing fresh air and coming into contact with a serene environment, this tranquil and simple life has tightly gripped my heart, which is disgusted with the city.

Indeed, rural life is filled with the vitality of youth. Although the rural economy has fallen to the point of collapse, this heavy grayness cannot obscure the active vigor. The beautiful smiles of healthy village girls and the sincere rustic tales of old farmers are all poetic scenes, the beauty of life!

This poetic rebirth, may you forever bind my weary soul!

(2) Lingering Autumn

The deep autumn wind reddened the maple leaves in front of the pavilion and brought the chill of early winter. Autumn is waning!

The sky is piled with large chunks of clouds, gray and heavy clouds, as if pressing on people's shoulders. In the fields, the withered yellow mulberry leaves and haggard rice stalks fully display the listlessness after being exploited by the landlords. Leafless branches sway in the wind, and withered leaves fall into the autumn stream. A lost lamb, in the quiet and desolate air, calls out to its dear mother. A lone goose, singing a sad tune, is searching for its final resting place.

This lingering autumn scene entered my eyes and resonated in my ears. My heart is stirred by an uneasy feeling, a bleak mood, and a melancholy thought.

"Autumn" is a season of sorrow. "Lingering Autumn" reveals the sadness of withering. All declining phenomena suggest the ruthlessness of "autumn." It generally makes people feel sad and despondent.

The deep autumn wind reddened the maple leaves in front of the pavilion and brought the chill of early winter. Autumn is disappearing on the heartstrings of sorrow.

Four Northeastern Company Commanders 254

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 20: Divination Brings Auspicious Omens, the Old Man Smiles for Days, Dispelling Endless Worries; Old Friends Live Across the Street

Ms. Jiang saw that he lowered his head and walked into the courtyard step by step, pushed the door open, stepped in with one foot, and still turned his head to look behind, with a hesitant expression. Ms. Jiang said: Who's outside? Chai Zhi said: No one. As he spoke, he walked in, first sighed silently, and then slowly sat down in the chair. Ms. Jiang's two eyebrows were tightly furrowed, almost forming a line. She thought to herself that when he went out just now, he was happy and excited, how come he came back with such a bitter face again? So, she put on an ignorant look and smiled at him: Is there any extra material? Gui Zhi said: No extra. He sat sideways, slightly raising his head to look at the sky outside the window. Ms. Jiang said: Did that tailor Wang say something to you? Gui Zhi still looked at the sky and did not say anything. Ms. Jiang said: I see you look a little unhappy, did tailor Wang say something to offend you? Gui Zhi suddenly twisted his body and said: Ugh! Why are you so nagging? We are taking him business as a tailor, that's looking up to him, why would he offend me if I didn't say anything strange? Ms. Jiang originally thought that because he looked angry, she wanted to ask him a few questions and then comfort him. Unexpectedly, the more she asked, the worse it got, and he became angry instead. She originally wanted to continue asking, but when she wanted to continue asking, she was afraid that he would become even more angry, so she just smiled at the girl and went to the inner room, no longer asking about the girl's affairs. But Gui Zhi himself did not relieve his distress because his mother did not pay attention to him. He thought to himself that in these few months, he had not received a letter from Gan Zhi. I thought he had forgotten me. But judging from his inquiries about me to the old woman, it is clear that he still pays attention to me. I am now a woman with a husband, and I am about to get married. I really don't want to see him sick and cause me a lot of trouble. (274)

Local Customs Notes

Birds and Insects 255

— Zhu Yu

During this season of falling leaves, the so-called paradise of Suzhou, birds and insects, are once again on the market to provide a pastime for the general leisure class. I have written down the general situation of this bird and insect life, which can also be regarded as a kind of Suzhou local customs note.

▲ Birds In spring, birds sing, and birds are originally animals that adorn the spring; orioles across the leaves and swallows through the flowers have long been praised and admired by poets, who consider them to be wonderful animals with poetic beauty. However, the birds on the market these days do not rely on their charming warbles to win people's appreciation. They rely on their agile flight and flexible feeding. When the food is thrown upwards by the bird players, the birds flap their wings and fly away, catching the food in the air, to win the joy of the bird players. There are about three types of birds that eat flying food, which are written below:

Baotou: This bird is about the size of a small crow, with soft light gray feathers all over its body and a wide yellow beak. Its flying power is the strongest among birds that eat flying food. The food of the Baotou is raw watermelon seeds. A well-trained bird can fly in the air non-stop to catch food and never tire. It is very beautiful to see it rising and falling like a rabbit and falcon.

Mala, its body is about the size of a chick, and its feathers are yellow and black, mottled and beautiful. It is a bird that eats millet. Although its flying power is not as durable as the Baotou, its colored feathers reflected in the clear sky are very dazzling when flying in the air.

Yellow Finch, the shape of the yellow finch is similar to that of a sparrow, but the light yellow and black feathers are much more beautiful than sparrows. It can not only fly and catch food, but also sing crisp songs in a bird cage to win people's joy. The food of the yellow finch is the dried seeds of perilla in medicine. It is flexible, but its flying power is relatively weak.

Among the three types of birds, Baotou is the most expensive and yellow finch is the cheapest. The method of training flying birds is to first starve the bird to be trained. When it is extremely hungry, tie a thin rope around the bird's neck and lure it to fly over to eat. When it approaches, throw the food into the air. Because it is hungry, it cannot help but flap its wings and fly away, opening its mouth to welcome the food. By training it slowly in this way, the bird's eyesight and skills gradually become skilled. When it is trained to perfection, it will habitually obey and listen to people's teasing. However, because these birds are excessively tortured, most of them cannot survive the winter. As the saying goes, "birds die for food," which is indeed a true saying.

▲ Insects Although many insects that chirp in autumn have fallen silent like cicadas in this season of withered grass and fallen leaves, the chirping crickets are flapping their wings and baring their fangs, displaying their mighty general power. The place where crickets are fought is called the "cricket shed." It is said that the amount of money won or lost in cricket fighting is quite large. The custom of cricket fighting was the pastime of Jia Sidao, the Taiping Prime Minister of the Song Dynasty, in the Hule Garden. But because the prime minister was a great man of the times, he called out loudly, and those below followed suit, which became a special kind of gambling among the people. The article "Cricket" recorded in "Strange Tales from a Chinese Studio" can give a glimpse of the situation of cricket fighting in the Song Dynasty.

There are also several rules for the method of fighting crickets: First, the weight of the cricket must be weighed on a scale, and it must be equal in weight before the fight can begin. However, there are also crickets that differ in weight, then the larger side must be allowed to give in a little, but this is rare. Second, is the betting method. The kind of money bet in the cricket arena is called flowers. In the past, the price of one flower was about one corner of the ocean, but now the most common flower costs half a yuan or one yuan per bet. The money bet on cricket fighting increases as the winter deepens, with as much as three or four thousand yuan per game. As for the method of fighting crickets, first put the crickets of both sides into a specially prepared battle fence. The shape and size of the fence is similar to a piano on a table, divided into two compartments, each with bamboo supports running through it, loosely barred. After the crickets arrive in the cage, they rest slightly, and then the person in charge of the fight removes the partition in the middle, so that the crickets on both sides fight each other. At that time, the crickets, due to the instigation of the fighter, will not hesitate to kill each other. After the first victory or defeat is decided, the defeated cricket is assigned to the resting compartment, covered with a wet towel on the fence to allow it to regain its spirit and try a second fight. If the loser in the second fight can turn defeat into victory, then it must rest again and make a third fight to determine the final victory, otherwise, after two fights, the victory or defeat of both sides is determined.

Page 13

Free Talk

Reflections on Reading History 256

— Cao Juren

The historian Van Loon, in explaining the French Revolution, said: "Regarding the French Revolution, whether you read a novel, watch a play, or a movie, it is very easy to get the impression that the revolution was created by thugs in the slums of Paris. In reality, this is not the case at all. ... Some happy but careless people use firecrackers as a game until the sparks fall down and pass through the cracks in the floor (this floor, like the rest of the building, is already old and rotten), and unfortunately fall on the bottom layer, where there are many years of old waste mixed together. Afterwards, everyone shouted loudly that there was a fire. But the owner of this house pays attention to nothing but managing his property and does not know how to put out the flames. The flames quickly spread and burned the entire building. We call this flame the French Revolution." This passage can be used as the best annotation for the idiom "people's hearts think of chaos." There is also a famous British figure, Chesterfield, who said twenty-five years before the French Revolution (1763): "All the phenomena that occurred before the great revolution and great chaos that I have seen in history are now present in France and are increasing day by day." "Everything is ready, only the east wind is lacking" is a more direct annotation of "people's hearts think of chaos."

When society is infected with a critical illness, "concealment" and "anesthesia" will never be effective. The first thing to do is to ask a doctor to carefully diagnose, prescribe medicine; the illusion that a magical talisman can cure the disease should be woken up from. The destruction of political power in Chinese history generally takes two forms: one is that the peasants who have reached the end of their rope gather together and burn down the old palaces like wildfire; the other is that foreign nations, like floods, completely destroy the old dikes. "People's hearts think of chaos" is certainly a social abnormality. Upon careful consideration, can we deny this abnormality? Enduring hardship and humiliation, like the peasants of China, can be said to be extreme; but there must always be a path for them to take. If the peasants have no path to take, and they believe that the "True Son of Heaven" is about to be born, then there is nothing to do! Moreover, if a nation does not have the courage to compete for survival and always plans to be content with the present, even if people's hearts do not think of chaos, what can be done!

China's chaos has been going on for a long time, and we should quickly find ways to eliminate the hearts of the people who think of chaos.

Secret Revealed 257

— Sheng Fu

I don't know where the greatest amusement park in China is? But some people say it is "The Great World." The Great World often makes contributions to society. What was the greatest contribution of 1933? It is said to be the big mooncake that cannot be eaten made during the Mid-Autumn Festival and this "secret revealed."

The "secret" that was "revealed" this time is "two strange people": "one with three feet" and "one with a tail." They just happened to be two brothers, born so "odd." Perhaps because they are a bit extraordinary, it is said that they have always been "strictly secretive." Although it once caused a sensation throughout Shandong Province, they never deigned to satisfy the eyes of their fellow villagers and lightly expose "that extra thing." However, strange people are always soft-hearted. This time, after "the world's persuaders repeatedly requested," they could not refuse and had to "reluctantly" satisfy the eyes of Shanghai's young masters and ladies.

However, this is what the advertisement says.

The advertisement also found a pair of portraits, with the caption: "No imitation," much like the scissors of "Genuine Wang Mazi." I don't pay attention to these things. I think that even if there is "no imitation," it is just a kind of physiological abnormality, a kind of "superfluous" disease. Not worth appreciating. What I regret is that "their" "secret" is not two big ears hanging down to the shoulders, but a pig's tail, which cannot inspire respect.

In addition, I also thought about the meaning of the word "reveal."

According to the advertisement, the "reveal" of this "secret" is passive, and I very much believe it. The reason is very obvious: "Who would want to show their tail?" The reason why they had no choice was for money. People with money can naturally "treasure" their tail and "reveal" other people's to have fun, and they also have to recognize this "tail" as a spectacle!

The painter's model, the one who "reveals" her "secret" is the painter. In China, the models are all poor girls. Naturally, it is also passive. Ladies with money are unwilling to do this business.

Also, a robber commits a crime, and this crime is naturally a "secret." The stolen owner and the robber have to stand in two different positions. The former wants to "reveal" this "secret," while the latter wants to keep it a secret. But there are also those who, because they cannot stand the master's beating, "reveal" this "secret" in a flurry of flesh and blood.

Therefore, people who "reveal" "secrets" must be powerful people, and those who are revealed are naturally the weak.

Then, is the "secret" so mysterious? Not necessarily. There are many in history who willingly "reveal secrets" to gain the laughter of their masters. In old dramas, there is a trick of "presenting a map," which is a traitor revealing the "secret" of his country's territory to the enemy. This is naturally not out of "being unable to refuse" and the pain of physical torture, because at that time the enemy had not yet penetrated deeply and the outcome of the battle had not yet been determined. But it is also not out of economic oppression, because the person who "presents a map" cannot be a small commoner, but must be at least a senior official, and senior officials all have money. So, what are they doing it for? I think there is no need for us to answer this! However, we must know that what they reveal is not a personal secret, and there is nothing as shameful as taking off their pants and showing their tail. What they reveal is the public; and it is also the public who suffer. Moreover, all of this is done in the dark, and you can't even see their own tail, only hearing sweet words and tears like springs, this is the real secret! Who will "reveal" this "secret"?

Chaliapin and Gorky 258

— Qi Ying

The day before yesterday, after reading Mr. Shi Zhecun's "Chaliapin in the Revolutionary Era," I couldn't help but have a few small thoughts.

Mr. Shi seems very worried about Chaliapin. If the concern is that the "Don Quixote," starring this world-renowned Russian singer, will not be understood or welcomed by the Shanghai audience, then that is indeed something to worry about. Wasn't this film only shown at the Nanjing Grand Theatre for four days, and wasn't it said that it didn't sell as well as the "New Woman" that followed it?

But what Mr. Shi is worried about is about Chaliapin as a person, as if he is easily misunderstood because some people, when criticizing this film, said that Chaliapin was once very famous in the Russian aristocratic theater. And Mr. Shi feels that the meaning of this sentence can easily suggest to readers that Chaliapin is a singer who served the aristocracy.

Is Chaliapin really such a singer? Mr. Shi says no, because Chaliapin, in Mr. Shi's words, is an artist who "not only was for the aristocracy, but also for the common people," and "should be said to be for humanity."

Coincidentally, I once saw an article in a magazine that was also about Chaliapin, titled "Chaliapin: Mask and Man"; and the main point of this article is exactly the opposite of Mr. Shi's, mainly exposing how Chaliapin is a base, greedy, deceptive singer who serves the aristocracy.

In fact, Chaliapin's current life, owning millions of wealth and living comfortably in a luxurious Parisian villa with the nobles and priests of St. Petersburg, isn't that the most eloquent explanation of whether Chaliapin is a singer who serves the aristocracy?

True, Chaliapin, like Gorky, went through a poor, oppressed, and wandering life. He also sympathized with poor young students and lived in his homeland for some time after the October Revolution, performing in workers' theaters. But these do not prevent Chaliapin from being a His Majesty's Solist, a singer who serves the aristocracy, because his true sympathy was on the side of the Tsarist aristocracy. He gave the Tsar, princes, generals, and even the theater director the greatest flattery. He received a gold watch from the Tsar and once even knelt on stage publicly to the Tsar, who had come to watch the play, although he only admitted to kneeling on one knee. This incident aroused indignation among some of his friends, or even broke off relations with him. Plekhanov returned the photo that Chaliapin had given him because of this, writing on it: "Returned because it is useless." Even the more docile artist Serov wrote to him, saying: "What a pity, even you finally crawled on the ground, you should be ashamed!" In order to express a little apology to his friends, Chaliapin once feigned refusal to attend the tercentenary banquet of the Romanov Dynasty.

After the revolution, the reason why Chaliapin was willing to associate with the workers, and even did not hesitate to praise the emerging forces, was only for the security and safety of his own life. The workers honestly believed that Chaliapin was their artist, willing to save on food and clothing to supply the insatiable needs of this artist. But they were deceived. Chaliapin finally came up with a clever excuse and slipped away from his homeland, returning forever to the arms of the aristocracy he served.

Even so, there was a deep friendship between this generation of singers who served the aristocracy, Chaliapin, and the great writer Gorky. Chaliapin still praises Gorky to the highest degree, thanking Gorky for the help and noble artistic influence he gave him. As for their initial acquaintance and their childhood friendship, Mr. Shi has given a brief introduction, and I won't go into detail here. I will only talk about how these two great artists, who came from the same background, took different paths, and how their friendship presented an inevitable crack.

On January 9, 1905, when the streets of St. Petersburg were filled with corpses and overflowing with human blood, to see how these two artists reacted to this incident, one only needs to look at the following words that Chaliapin said in his book "Mask and Man," published in Paris in 1932:

"He (referring to Gorky) was pale and agitated.

'They are slaughtering innocent people, those villains!'

Although I was still singing at a noble's banquet that night, I felt that the truth was on Gorky's side."

The truth was on Gorky's side, but this did not stop him from singing at the nobles' banquets! And maybe he sang very well too!

After the "truth" was finally proved to be "on Gorky's side," Chaliapin ran to a foreign country, which made Gorky angry. He once wrote a letter to Chaliapin, persuading him to return. Regarding this matter, Chaliapin wrote in the same book:

"Later, when I went to Rome, Alexei Maximovich [Gorky's name] said to me again, telling me that I must return to my homeland. Once again, and more firmly, I refused, telling him that I didn't want to go there... When I later took reasonable steps because I refused to go back, this greatly broke our friendship... I don't want to hide it, I say it with great emotion, losing Gorky was very sad and painful for me."

In fact, Chaliapin doesn't have to be sad and painful. Gorky's friendship was no longer necessary for him. He could no longer gain instruction from Gorky. ………

Two Brothers (6) (6) 259

— Translated by Maupassant Li Weike

"Don't you remember that day on the "Pearl" fishing boat you wanted to row more forcefully than me? Don't you remember all the flattering words you said in front of her? But the result made you die of jealousy! Later, when I got this property, you became even more crazy, so you hated me, and you expressed your hatred in various ways. You made everyone suffer, and you never stopped spitting out the bile that suffocated you."

Pier clenched his two fists, wishing he could jump on him and strangle his throat:

"Ah! Shut your beak, don't talk about this property again!"

Jean shouted again

"But jealousy is seeping out of your skin. Not a single word you said to your father, mother, or me did not contain jealousy. Because you were jealous, you pretended to look down on me! Because you were jealous, you tried to quarrel with everyone. And now that I'm rich, you can't stand it anymore, you've become poison, you're tormenting our mother, as if it's her fault!..."

Pier kept retreating to the fireplace, his lips half-open, his eyes wide, he had the kind of rage that could make people commit crimes. He repeated in a lower but panting voice:

"Shut your beak, shut your beak!"

"I've wanted to tell you what I've been thinking for a long time; you've given me this opportunity now, so you're drinking poison yourself. I loved"

A woman! You know this, and you mock her in front of me, you've forced me to a dead end; so you're drinking poison yourself. But if you do it again, I'll smash those poisonous teeth of yours! I'll force you to respect me."

"Respect you, me?"

"That's right, respect me!"

"Respect you... you... you who have disgraced our family for your greed?"

"What did you say? Say it again... say it again, okay?..."

"I said that no one would accept someone else's property if it meant becoming someone else's son."

Jean stood still, unmoving, he didn't understand his words, he was panicked by the implication of his words:

"What? What did you say... say it again, okay?"

"I said that everyone is whispering, everyone is spreading the word, saying that you are the son of the person who left you the property. Listen carefully, a self-respecting child would not accept money that would tarnish his mother's reputation."

"Pier... Pier... Pier... you even thought of this? ...You... said such insulting words?"

"That's right... I... this is what I said. Haven't you noticed how heartbroken I've been for a month? I don't sleep all night, and I hide like a beast during the day; I'm in so much pain and shame that I don't even know what I'm saying, what I'm doing, or what I'll become, because I only guessed at first, but now I understand."

"Pier... shut up... Mom is in the next room! She'll hear us... she'll hear us."

But he had to get his thoughts off his chest! So he told everything, his suspicions, his speculations, his internal struggles, the certainty he had gained, and the story of the portrait that had been lost and found again.

New York Stock Market Slightly Down 266

New Feng Yang Line Reported That on the 20th, the New York Stock Market Was Driven Small by All Stocks Because Special Stocks That Are Often Manipulated by Speculative Companies, Such as United Bag Paper and Atlas Tack, Fell Sharply by About $10 Again Under the Pressure of Sellers at Noon, With a Slight Rise Back Afterwards. Speculators Paid No Attention to Good and Bad Commercial News, But Were Uniquely Concerned About Various Things That Were Unfavorable to the Market, Including the Inspection of the Work of Speculative Companies, the Possibility of Government Supervision of the Exchange, and the Appreciation of the US Dollar Due to the Fixed Gold Price, Etc. The Total Number of Transactions for the Day Was 2.16 Million Shares. "Wheat" Fell Terribly by 0.3 Points. Due to the Disappearance of Famous Speculator Jesse Livermore, the Police Authority Believed He Was Kidnapped, and Because Soviet Russia Had 225,000,000 Bushels of Wheat That Could Be Exported, the Longs Tended to Sell. The Department of Agriculture Estimated That the Condition of Winter Wheat on December 1 Was 74.3 Per Hundred, Compared to 68.9 Percent Last Year. "Cotton" Had No Trend, and It Was Expected That There Would Be No New Developments Before Congress Convenes. However, Wall Street Believes That Consumer Needs Will Definitely Increase After the New Year. The Financial Rehabilitation Society Bought Gold, and the Price Per Tael Was $34.06, Unmoved. Shantou: 23, Inland: 151, Jiangxi: 25, Luzhou: 10, Nanjing: 5

The cotton market's downward trend is gradually emerging due to the approaching end of the year, tight financial conditions, and higher cotton prices compared to yarn prices. Factory demand is quite sluggish, as there is no outlet for yarn, making it difficult to purchase raw materials. Consequently, the spot cotton market price is lower than the futures price. Another explanation is that the Pu Yi Factory is still hesitant about receiving goods. Daily factory inventories of cotton yarn are increasing, cotton imports are particularly sluggish, and there are still concerns about falling prices of Indian cotton.

Grain: Futures Flour and Wheat See Sharp Decline 274

After the opening of the flour market this morning, all months showed a consistent downward trend. Foreign wheat quotations in Chicago fell by eight jiao to one yuan, and in Canada, they fell by approximately twelve jiao. Therefore, at the opening, sentiment was already weak. Currently, the market trend is that although the government has announced a tax increase on foreign wheat, in reality, the tax increase and market consumption cannot be integrated. Moreover, after the tax increase, the pricing of foreign wheat is cheaper than before, which is unexpected by most people. Therefore, although trading is not brisk, the market has already declined. By the time the afternoon session opened, market sentiment for all months remained weak and unsustainable. Outside investors were eager to sell, predicting that the trend for current foreign wheat would still be low prices. The market's inability to stand firm is likely still influenced by international surpluses. This month's price fell by three fen compared to the previous day, January fell by two and a half fen, February and March fell by two fen and two and a half li, April fell by four fen, and May fell by three and a half fen.

After the opening of the wheat market this morning and afternoon, the market for all months suddenly showed a sharp decline. Foreign wheat quotations in Chicago fell by approximately eight jiao to one yuan, and in Canada, they fell by approximately twelve jiao. Therefore, after the opening, sentiment was already negatively affected. The opening prices for all months fell invisibly by five to six fen. By the time the afternoon session opened, prices fell by another four to five fen. The cause of the decline was partly due to the receivers for this month slightly hedging far-term contracts. A certain trader had two to three thousand tons of foreign wheat in hand and took the opportunity to sell. However, with few buyers in the market and inland traders inactive, the selling pressure increased, resulting in a sharp decline. As a result, February fell sharply by one jiao and one fen compared to the previous day. March and April fell by one jiao, and the remaining months did not open. Spot wheat did not open due to factory demand being inactive and standards also falling sharply.

Late Rice Shows Slight Weakness 275

(South Shanghai) Sources from various merchant groups numbered over 50 (7,000-8,000 shi), with late rice still scarce, accounting for nearly 20. The movement and purchasing of bagged rice by visiting merchants have also virtually stopped. This is because the Winter Solstice festival is approaching according to the lunar calendar, so even if they buy, it is only in small quantities. Therefore, most of the rice sold recently has been stored in upper-level warehouses. Consequently, although sellers want to tighten prices due to the scarcity of goods, it is ultimately difficult to achieve, resulting in a flat market condition with a hint of weakness. It is estimated that the market sold over 2,000 bags yesterday, with visiting merchants accounting for only 400-500 bags. The sales of various japonica and Du Yang long-grain rice are still good, but market conditions remain stable. Demand from distilleries for yeast-transformed rice is quite strong, and market sentiment has risen by one chi.

(North Shanghai) Sources from various routes numbered 58-59. Sales of various goods in the market are slow. Prices for white japonica, Yang Du, and visiting merchants' long-grain rice are down several fen. Thin rice and yeast-transformed rice are stable.

Visiting Xian Rice Depreciates but Sells Well 276

Recently, arrivals of visiting Xian rice have gradually increased. Due to the price increase at the beginning of the month, various regions have been transporting rice to Shanghai. Currently, Shanghai's inventory has exceeded 150,000 bags, and the quantity of goods en route or about to arrive is also considerable. However, when this batch arrived in Shanghai, the regular rice warehouses had no transactions, and traders were anxious and eager to sell. Yesterday, various parties dumped and sold at reduced prices, causing prices to fall by about half a jiao. Only after the price reduction did local merchants inquire. Half of the sales in this street went to speculators who were looking for opportunities to stockpile. The visiting rice mostly belonged to the Fuzhou merchant group. The transactions in this street involved over 1,200 bags of Ji Yuan, Ji Zao, Ji Wan, Ji You, Ji Jing, and Bao Zao rice. The Fuzhou merchants bought a total of 1,500 bags of unpolished Jing, You, Hong, and Shashi unpolished rice, as well as Mingguang polished rice. Other visiting merchant groups did not inquire about the goods.

Amoy Merchants Increase Purchases of Red Grain 277

Since the new crop of red grain entered the market, the trend has been stable, and the supply has not surged. It is currently estimated that there are around 20 trucks. In addition to sales to inland regions, yesterday, Amoy merchants purchased one truck of new red husked grain at a price of 3.05 yuan, and three trucks of Chong red husked grain at a price of 2.95 yuan. There were no changes in the market. Yesterday was the first time the Amoy merchants purchased new crop grain, with some transactions in old crop grain, but the trading volume was only 100-200 bags, so the market did not pay much attention.

Silk and Tea: Overseas Silk Prices Decline Across the Board 279

(Lackluster Sales of Foreign Silk) Overseas raw silk markets are experiencing strong selling pressure from Japanese silk, and general holders of spot silk are actively selling as foreign exchange rates lengthen. As a result, silk prices in New York and Lyon have declined across the board. Both Chinese and foreign silk merchants in Shanghai are adopting a negative attitude, and the silk market is quiet. Yesterday, 25 bales were distributed to local silk factories such as Daohuang and Baichang, with prices remaining flat and weak.

(20 Dan of Double Cocoon Silk Transported to Hunan) Sales of double cocoon silk have been slow to improve. Inland buyers of cotton for stripping are making sporadic purchases. Yesterday, 20 dan of double cocoon silk were transported by small boat to Pinghu, Hunan, for use in cotton stripping.

(Artificial Silk Sales Increasingly Stagnant) Due to tight foreign exchange rates, it is difficult for artificial silk prices to fall. As the end of the year approaches, financial conditions are extremely tight, and sales are increasingly stagnant. Yesterday, only 18 boxes of current and futures goods of Yunmeiwen and other imported Kaili brand Samsung and other brands were sold, with prices ranging from 182.75 yuan to 173.25 yuan net.

Business Experience (51)

Domestic Sea Shrimp Holds Exclusive Advantage 280

— Xinsheng

Sea shrimp, also written as sea shrimp, is a type of small fish produced in coastal waters. "Yinxian Zhi": "Yin has a small fish, its taste is like dried shrimp, commonly called sea shrimp." "Bei Hu Lu": "Enzhou produces goose feather shrimp, preserved in salt, as thin as hair, with an exceptionally delicious taste." This is the origin of the name sea shrimp. However, it is usually written as "sea swallow" or "sea salt," which is actually incorrect. According to "sea swallow," it is a migratory bird (i.e., swallow) that must cross the sea to reach warm regions, hence the name sea swallow. Ancient people said, "Sea swallows nest in pairs on玳瑁梁 [tortoiseshell beams]," referring to this type of swallow. "Sea salt" is a county name, belonging to Zhejiang Qiantang Road. Therefore, writing "sea shrimp" as "sea swallow" or "sea salt" is not only different in pronunciation but also vastly different in meaning and cannot be interchanged. Here, I am the first to point this out to correct the common errors. (Editor's note: also written as sea salted)

Sea shrimp can be roughly divided into two types: (1) "Coarse Cinnamon" or "Medium Cinnamon," about one inch long (those longer than one inch are called coarse cinnamon, those less than one inch are called medium cinnamon), with fine scales, a thicker head, a golden-yellow back, and a slightly bluish-white belly; the taste is fresh. (2) Fine Cinnamon, four to five fen long, with a light yellow body, scales so fine they are indistinguishable, and a taste even more delicious than the former. (The word "cinnamon" is a substitute name for sea shrimp; people in the trade often refer to it as "cinnamon" instead of "sea shrimp.")

The Shanghai market sells both Japanese and domestic goods. Japanese goods are produced in places like Fuji; domestic goods are produced in several places: Ningbo 新化, Jiangshan 温州, Yantai, Weihaiwei, etc. The biggest disadvantage of Japanese sea shrimp is that it is bland and tasteless; its advantage is that it is lighter in weight and has fewer head crumbs. Smaller merchants often stock Japanese goods for retail convenience; however, from the consumer's point of view, taste is naturally the priority. Therefore, in order to meet customer demand, merchants must also consider stocking domestic goods in moderate quantities. As a result, domestic sea shrimp can still hold an exclusive advantage in the market, looking down on inferior goods. As for the different grades of domestic sea shrimp, the best is the fine cinnamon produced in the Beichu ocean area of Ningbo (there is also a single-top and double-tip type, with the double-tip being finer and more uniform, which is the highest grade). The next best is produced in Huangqi and Wushan. The goods produced in Xinhua and Jiangshan, whether fine cinnamon or coarse cinnamon, are also very good. Wenzhou sea shrimp (both fine and coarse types) are of good quality and affordable prices, and are the most common. The goods produced in Yantai and Weihaiwei have the advantages of Japanese goods, but also the disadvantages of Japanese goods, which is a pity. However, they are sufficient to replace Japanese goods and meet the demand.

China's coastline is several times longer than Japan's, yet many marine products must be imported from Japan, which is thought-provoking. In fact, there are many things that, if developed and promoted, would be sufficient to rival Japanese goods in both quantity and quality and meet the needs of the Chinese people. Sea shrimp is one such product. The reporter sincerely hopes that merchants in the industry and consumers who need it will pay close attention!

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

A Must-Read Book for Young People - The Spring and Autumn Annals 301

— Wei Ba

The matter of "New Book Recommendations" is, it is said, quite fashionable in today's literary world, and some have even engaged in extensive written disputes over it. This has prompted me to bring out an old book that has long been stored in my mind, wanting to join in the excitement and "recommend it" to the general literary youth of today.

Upon stating the name of the book to be recommended, no one will find it strange, it is such a familiar name. What is strange is the point on which its application is broad, yet it is never noticed.

That is none other than our Master Kong’s (Confucius) own great work, "The Spring and Autumn Annals."

This is truly a good book that only those "born with knowledge" can create. Although it records the historical events of rise and fall over 242 years, it actually contains the essence of the "Chinese people." Reading it can not only help with writing, but also serve as a foundation for being a person.

I have often argued that when people write today, they often make mistakes. Half of the reason is due to environmental factors, but the other half is largely due to the authors not having read "The Spring and Autumn Annals."

Writing abhors directness, as directness easily pricks others' wounds. The principles of "The Spring and Autumn Annals" are: "Subtle and gentle." "Subtle" means not abandoning one's own position, while "gentle" means not offending the other party. Sometimes it contains hidden satire, and sometimes it subtly protects; this is truly the secret to being a person and writing well throughout the ages.

Therefore, it is clear that it is ridiculing the emperor for sending envoys to mourn the concubine of a feudal lord, which is inappropriate, but "The Spring and Autumn Annals" says: "The Heavenly King sent the steward Xuan to return the funeral gifts of Zhongzi of Duke Hui." The writing is so gentle. It is clear that the feudal lords are summoning the king, but "The Spring and Autumn Annals" says: "The Heavenly King hunted in Heyang." The cover-up is so strict. These are all the subtle and profound meanings of the ancient sages, and the modern terms such as "shortening the front lines" and "already understood" are probably derived from here.

Furthermore, China is a country of "rites and morals," and "The Spring and Autumn Annals" is even more a textbook of rites and morals. The so-called "one word of praise is more glorious than the finest robes; one word of condemnation is more severe than an axe," is enough to make "rebellious ministers and treacherous sons" fear in their hearts.

Zheng Qiao's commentary on "The Spring and Autumn Annals" states: "In general, if 'The Spring and Autumn Annals' records a person's goodness, then people throughout the ages will point to them as a good person; if it records their evil, then people throughout the ages will point to them as an evil person." Therefore, the good and evil deeds of the rulers and ministers over 242 years cannot escape the 18,000 words. The pen is so powerful that people thousands of years later still feel chills down their spines upon hearing it. This kind of writing has now been learned by some people and is already being tested. They come up with many posthumous titles, such as "laborious and meritorious," "extremely heinous," and so on, to add to the people they want to target. However, whether this kind of writing can be as respected as Master Kong's masterpiece "The Spring and Autumn Annals" in the thousands of years to come, making people feel chills down their spines upon seeing it, is not yet known. In short, this is also a writing style that is worth emulating and should undoubtedly be paid attention to by modern literary youth.

Secondly, the great principle of "respecting the king and expelling the barbarians," which is a self-praising and self-aggrandizing idea, must also be known.

China is a country of "rites and morals," so apart from the word "name," which must be fought for, everything else can be resolved through "kingly ways." Confucius said, "The instruments of state cannot be lent to others," which is not only the words of a "sage," but also the words of all Chinese people. Therefore, although the Zhou dynasty was declining, it must be respected; although the barbarians were strong, they must be suppressed. At the end of "The Spring and Autumn Annals," there was only a fragmented "Old Zhou Shop" that was barely holding on, but it still had to put on a brave face and respect it as the "royal family." And towards the powerful state of Chu, which was threatening China, it used terms like "Jing," "Chu," "person," and "son" to indicate that it was not the same as China. Although at that time, many members of the Zhou royal family and descendants of the Tang and Yu dynasties were indeed destroyed by the strong state of Chu, our Master Kong always adhered to the principle of "not engaging in any relationship in writing" and "not recognizing" them. Although this policy could not save the various states from the disaster of destruction at the time, it seems to be successful now.

Page 16

Didn't Chu and the other states disappear now? "Please see those who destroy others, their own country will also be destroyed," but Chu was given a "condemnation" by Master Kong, a condemnation that still makes people feel regret when they read "The Spring and Autumn Annals." Doesn't justice therefore remain between heaven and earth? Therefore, this kind of writing is also worth learning, at least it can comfort oneself under the serious national crisis.

Furthermore, Hu Anguo said, "Understand 'The Spring and Autumn Annals,' and then one can weigh the affairs of the world." There are so many people who want to "weigh the affairs of the world" now, so "recommending" this "Spring and Autumn Annals," which has been ridiculed as "broken court reports," is not only enough to help with writing and serve as a foundation for being a person.

China Possesses the "Magic of a Beautiful Woman" 302

— Qiong Sheng

In the past few months, our China has had Bernard Shaw's "round-the-world trip" to visit, with Malraux passing through and investigating, and recently, the French novelist Colette has followed in the footsteps of Shaw and Malraux to tour our great country. These people are either veterans of the literary world or famous celebrities and writers, which shows that China can truly be said to be a place where all nations come to pay tribute, and "literary stars are shining brightly"!

According to reports, Colette was "captivated for several days" by the singer Xue Yanqin in the Confucius Temple in Nanjing. After developing a fondness for the old capital, the "center of past dynasties," in Beijing, he hurriedly departed for Japan without saying goodbye. However, he has been a bachelor for decades and can be said to be "free from worldly desires," but upon arriving in China, he was unable to escape, being captivated wherever he went, filled with a dream of marrying a "humorous Chinese woman with Oriental beauty to comfort his life." Only because of a warning from a "romantic female writer" that he did not win the favor of Chinese women, did he give up on Chinese women so resolutely? No; he only felt admiration for Chinese women, regretting that "they met too late and separated too quickly." How could he be discouraged by this? Before departing, he said, "The beauty of China is like the magic of a beautiful woman. If someone rejects this magic, they will surely regret it ten thousand years later." It can be seen that his affection is so strong that he probably wishes to be married to a Chinese woman for countless lifetimes, and, moreover, he cannot forget China! Therefore, after traveling in Japan, Colette will still return!

Indeed, in my opinion, China also has beauty like the magic of a beautiful woman, with Shanghai, the "Paris of the East," the ancient city that is the "center of past dynasties," and the beautiful women who "wear clothes as if wrapped around the body," and who are specially waiting for these foreign celebrities to enjoy. However, like our female writer's warning to Colette, although he praised "Oriental beauty" and "Chinese beauty" after attending banquets and receptions hosted by ministries and associations and interacting with our distinguished ladies, I am afraid he still lacks a deep understanding of "Chinese beauty" and "Oriental beauty."

China has magnificent mountains and rivers, inexhaustible and inexhaustible wealth, a mild and bright climate, and a "peaceful and honest" people. All of this has been praised by foreign "travelers" and "inspection groups." However, Colette only praised the ancient Guangdong, the ancient heart of prosperity, which shows that he still does not have a thorough understanding of "Chinese beauty." Chinese women have morals of "upholding propriety and righteousness," the gentleness of elegance and harmony, the clear teachings of the three obediences and four virtues, and the simplicity of marrying for virtue, not for appearance. However, Colette saw only the modern ladies who "wear clothes as if wrapped around the body" and thought they were "indescribably beautiful," further indicating that he does not have a deep understanding of the unique "Oriental beauty" of our country's women.

However, Colette is a novelist and has the demeanor of a literary figure. It is said that he is also very "humorous," and his "absurd and unfounded" remarks should be interpreted as humor. He compares China to a beautiful woman, and I believe it deserves the "beauty" that it possesses (not sensuality!). Furthermore, he says that "Chinese beauty" is like "the magic of a beautiful woman," which also symbolizes that China's current seductiveness is indeed extremely strong. This point, when examined in reality, is precisely the point. At the same time, since it is already a beautiful woman and also has magic, it is inevitable that it will cause many men to be infatuated and passionate. It is a matter of course that many politicians, military strategists, diplomats, and scientists and artists have recently come to China to "court" from afar and have also added various praises in our pleasant conversations, which is a glimpse of their state of being infatuated with "Chinese beauty." However, the "magic of a beautiful woman" is too great, and it is bound to cause the permissible "lovers" to fight for love, which will lead to unfortunate events before our eyes. Therefore, we should not be arrogant and conceited because Colette praises us as "beautiful" and having "magic." We must be vigilant against the unfortunate events caused by being too "beautiful and having magic"!

At the same time, although China has the "magic of a beautiful woman" and is rich in "Oriental beauty," after all, it is now a time when Europeanization and "modernity" are prevalent, and the temptation of material things is great, so it is inevitable that it will fall into the path of "degeneration." Today, one can talk about love with this "man," and tomorrow, one can marry another "man," and one can even use the "magic of a beautiful woman" to practice romanticism. Why not practice the sale of both body and soul? I advise Colette to turn back as soon as possible and not be too infatuated with our "Oriental beauty" and "the magic of a beautiful woman"!

Fallen Man 303

— A Qin

Ever since Old Master Zhao's family took in a daughter-in-law, he's been feeling rather vexed these past few days. The reason isn't exactly displeasure with his newly wedded daughter-in-law, but rather another matter arising from this joyous event.

Today, he's once again sitting in the accounting room, flipping through his rent rice ledger. It's because the new grain has long been brought in from the fields, but the rent rice coming in is still sparse.

He opened the first page, which read:

"Gu Shiguan household, farming ten mu, not yet returned." He was a bit displeased and casually flipped down;

"Chen Changsheng household, farming four mu, repaid old debts ten yuan, new rent outstanding."

"Li Erguan household, farming five mu, two harvests unpaid."

"Lu Ahu household, farming two mu, repaid old rent five yuan, paid new rent five yuan, balance outstanding."

"Shen Wensheng household, farming twelve mu, old debts fifteen yuan, new rent unpaid."

"Wang Jinbao household, farming seven mu, unpaid."

"Yang Atu household, farming fifteen mu, unpaid."

"............owing a certain amount."

"............unpaid."

After flipping through a few pages, he couldn't help but feel vexed again. He thought, "Life used to be so good. Rice sold for seven or eight yuan per shi, and each mu of farmland yielded at least six or seven yuan in rent. In one winter, the money would come in neatly by the thousands. Now, each mu of farmland only yields about four yuan, and there are still arrears every year. When collecting from them, they always say that farming folks are suffering, the harvest this year is bad, and the rice price is too low. They need to keep some rice at home for their wives, mothers, and children to survive. I'm tired of hearing these kinds of words. These people are truly hateful. Is it only farming that is hard? Are landowners not suffering in this era? You need to survive, but don't landlords need to survive? Hateful creatures, they should all be locked up!" The more Old Master Zhao thought, the angrier he became, and he threw the ledger onto the table.

Suddenly, a "grain certificate" fell out of the ledger unintentionally. He picked it up and looked at it, equally unintentionally. This further fueled his anger.

He read:

"Unified levy silver one tael five mace, with additional levy for autonomous district expenses two jiao five fen, education expenses one yuan, rural pacification donation two jiao, defense donation five jiao, road construction mu donation one yuan two jiao five fen, military surtax one yuan, peasant bank fund three jiao, airplane donation three jiao five, Party headquarters expenses four jiao five fen, rice special tax nine jiao, land survey fee five jiao, district office expenses four jiao five fen............" He thought, "Damn it! These dog officials, after eating their fill, only know how to come up with all kinds of new taxes. The official tax is one tael five mace, but the surtaxes and donations exceed it by more than twenty times. They don't care whether people can bear it or not, just shouting slogans like 'rural bankruptcy' and 'relief for rural areas,' but in reality, they act as if the current rural bankruptcy isn't enough, and they are doing everything to increase the burden on the owners. In the past, families who owned one or two hundred mu of land could be considered well-off. Apart from the year's expenses, they would always have a surplus of one or two thousand yuan at the end of the year. But now, it's impossible to get by without borrowing. But opening one's mouth to borrow money is embarrassing, and all the expenses cannot be reduced urgently. Just like this time, for my son's wedding, I spent more than ten thousand yuan. The daughter-in-law is from an old family, so all the customary rituals had to be observed as usual. Although outsiders say that my Zhao family is still doing well, who knows how much thought I've put into it? And like my second son, for the sake of family reputation, he has to study, and I have to pay eighteen hundred yuan in tuition every year. Alas, this situation is really not as good as in the past, and it seems like it's going to get worse............"

He collapsed wearily into the chair, unable to think any further.

Swearing Oaths 304

— Wei Ba

Swearing oaths is undoubtedly a kind of "national essence." The Analects records that our Confucius once went to see Nanzi, the wife of Duke Ling of Wei - a woman famous for her licentiousness - causing displeasure among his "unable to die a natural death" disciple, Zilu. Thereupon, our Old Master panicked, fearing that his straightforward disciple would say something unpleasant. He swore an oath, saying, "If I deny it, may Heaven forsake me! May Heaven forsake me!" to prove that his visit to Nanzi was not with any bad intentions. After this was said, Zilu naturally did not delve deeper, and so a comedy of discord between master and disciple passed by. Only ten characters were able to soften the heart of a man known for his "courage and fierce fighting," which shows a glimpse of the magical power of the two words "swearing oaths."

From then on, it has been passed down through the generations, revered as one of the "arts of getting along in the world." Whether it's high officials taking office or a neighbor losing a chicken, whenever there is internal shame or external suspicion, they must rely on these two words.

But the names may differ slightly. For example, the "official style" - or simply "official" - of swearing an oath is no longer called "swearing an oath," but "taking an oath." When taking an oath, one must invariably straighten one's clothes, solemn one's appearance, face the portrait of Sun Yat-sen, raise one's right hand, and read the printed oath. The oath says: "I solemnly and sincerely... If I violate this oath, I will accept the most severe punishment..." and so on. It is said that this is also a legal procedure that officials must go through, meaning to tell them that if they do wrong in the future, they cannot go back on their word. But in our memory, it seems that every official, when it is discovered that he already has the qualifications for "if I violate...", and is prepared to cash in on him, has mostly already wandered overseas or gone far away. As a result, this "most severe punishment" is often "undeliverable" due to "unknown address." There are probably many such dubious cases, and after some time, they can be sold as new goods again.

So, to put it bluntly, a rural woman's swearing oath is nothing more than lighting a few more incense sticks for the mud bodhisattvas in the City God Temple, and the swearing oath of high officials is just to join in the fun of the day! Otherwise, wouldn't it be too desolate!

All of these things, in essence, are the same. What was said earlier mostly concerns clarifying right and wrong, such as you saying I stole your chicken, and I saying I didn't steal it. If you still don't believe me, then I have to swear an oath, "If I stole your chicken, then I will be like this and like that." With "divine beings" as a guarantee, then you believe me. And what is being said now mostly belongs to hoping for the future, meaning to say, "Why don't you..." All of these words and phrases, at first glance, seem extremely generous, solemn, painful, and full of confidence; but upon closer thought, it is also felt that using one finger to point at the sun in the sky, and waving a hand with tears, saying "Destiny is like this, what more can be said" or saying with teeth chattering "In a few years, their country will naturally be like this and like that" is not easy to make people optimistic. On the contrary, it paints a picture of decline.

Page 17

The White Scar on Old Wen's Head 305

— Wen Bing

——Five Yuan to Buy a Hair Restraining Cap——

Old Wen had a lifelong regret, which was that he didn't know what year it was, but when he was just a toddler who could walk, he had a boil on his head that festered for three months before it slowly closed and scabbed over. But from then on, hair never grew again, leaving a white scar the size of a wine cup.

When Old Wen was eleven years old, he went to town to take the entrance exam for higher elementary school. It was early autumn, and still so hot. By this time, he was already somewhat aware of the unseemliness of the white scar, so he put on his winter melon-skin cap early. He also grew his hair long, hearing that there were Western-style barbershops in town. He was fully prepared to get a Western-style "slicked-back" hairstyle, which he thought would surely cover up the white scar. On his way, the autumn sun fiercely beat down on his melon-skin cap, and smoke and water steamed from his hair. Only then did he loosen his melon-skin cap. There were few passersby, so there was naturally no need to worry.

Entering the town, his eyes constantly darted around at the shops on both sides. From the beginning of the street to the end of the alley, there wasn't a single barbershop with a sign. All there were were shop assistants standing on the street with short benches, shaving people's heads bald. He felt very disappointed.

Because of this, during his years of schooling in town, except for the unbearable heat of midsummer, when he really couldn't wear a hat and had to "let it be," his only method and only comfort in all seasons was relying on a melon-skin cap. Fortunately, wearing a black satin melon-skin cap was still considered very fashionable in the small town, otherwise he would have been even more troubled.

Well, he finally arrived one day in the infinitely prosperous Shanghai, where you could buy even living statues if you had the money.

At this time, he was older, and his "love of beauty" and "shyness" grew in direct proportion to his age. His dislike of the white scar on his head naturally became even stronger. Moreover, he had long known that there were all kinds of enchanting female students in Shanghai's schools, so on the day he entered school, his first move was to go to the beauty salon across the street from the school, and get a Western-style "slicked-back" hairstyle. The barber applied a thick layer of Stacomb to him, and combed it again and again. He tilted his head, rolled his eyes, and looked in the mirror. Sure enough, the white scar was gone. He felt immense comfort, so much so that even though the sign originally said "Gentlemen's Haircut Two Dimes," he was so generous that he reached out and gave the barber "forty-eight cents." The barber smiled and respectfully saw him out of the shop, and to the street.

Old Wen usually didn't have such high spirits. He whistled all the way back to school, practically going crazy with joy. He slept soundly that night, and when he woke up the next day, he smoothed his hair and looked in the mirror. He found a white scar again. He knew this was the inevitable result of not applying Stacomb and not combing. But he didn't know what the stuff applied to the hair was called, so he secretly asked another classmate. Then he rushed to a foreign goods store and bought a bottle. He then thickly applied a layer and carefully combed and combed, but he still couldn't hide that annoying white scar. In the end, his own technique was not good.

Thus, Old Wen felt the same kind of trouble he had in the melon-skin cap era, but it was even more severe. Going to class, he secretly sat in the last row, afraid of being seen by the female students, which would be so embarrassing.

The time was also exactly early autumn, and wearing a hat properly would undoubtedly make people laugh at him even more.

Old Wen was distressed. He thought left and right, but couldn't find a suitable solution. Later, a kind classmate offered him an idea, saying that he should go to the fabric street near the Four Horse Road and spend two dimes to buy a hair-restraining cap. That would be the best solution. He could wear it often in the dormitory, and it wouldn't matter if he wore it to class. If he wanted to be so particular about etiquette, he could first press his hair with a hair-restraining cap, then apply Stacomb, and then comb. The white scar could surely be covered up.

Old Wen thought it was a great idea.

So he went to buy one. The price of the cap was set at two dimes, and he gave the vendor a five-yuan bill. The vendor couldn't make change, so he took it to exchange, but said it was a fake bill. After arguing and pulling for a long time, Old Wen still suffered a loss, took back the fake bill, and gave the vendor "twenty-eight cents."

Old Wen returned, discouraged, and said to his classmates:

"Bad luck, really bad luck, five yuan to buy a hair-restraining cap!"

Novel

Shanghai (II) (5) 307

— Zhang Laosan

(Thirty-Seven) Two People Who Don't Speak

Afterwards, Cousin left, and Sister Min saw her off for more than an hour. Upon returning, she organized clothes and other items alone in the bedroom, like someone about to leave on a long trip. I took a walk in the park for a while, walking through that newly paved sandy path. My heart felt even more uneasy. Returning to the company, my younger brother told me that my sister was going out. I hurried to the third floor. Sister Min buried her head in packing up small items. Seeing me step in, she raised her hands in a gesture of obstruction, saying:

"Don't come in, don't come in, I'm looking for something important."

"Xin Di said you're going out?" I really stopped in my tracks.

"Listen to what children say." Sister Min looked up, yawned, and said with a smile, as if she was very tired.

"Exactly what important thing did you lose, that you're searching the whole room? Tell me, I'll help you find it."

I stepped through the door and sat on a chair. The clothes hanging on the wall-mounted hangers were gone, and the other items on the writing desk in front of the window were also packed neatly. In any case, this situation was inconsistent with searching for items. Sister Min was still bent over, taking out a stack of shoe boxes from under the bed, throwing the broken ones out the door at random.

"Sister Min," I didn't expect the change to come so suddenly and quickly, and I supported her with both hands. "Sister Min, please tell me, your brother hasn't done anything wrong!"

"Who said you did something wrong?" She said and turned her head away, and I vaguely saw that her eyes were full of tears.

I closed the door, helped her sit on the bed, and pulled over a chair for myself.

"Sister, if you don't have anything to apologize for, you told me this, you can't let your brother feel sorry forever. Sister, speak up, sister."

Sister Min lowered her head, playing with a piece of broken cardboard from a box in her hand.

"Sister, we escaped from our hometown together. Is this kind of ending what you want now? If you want to leave, I can't force you, but you always have to give a reason..."

Sister Min raised her tearful eyes and handed me a crumpled piece of paper from her bag. It was the letter from Cousin returning my letter. I didn't know when it had been lost.

"Sister Min, you agreed when I wrote this letter. Today, Sister Hui returned it to me, and I casually stuffed it in my pocket. It doesn't matter if it's lost."

"Hmph, you went to Xujiahui without telling me, did I agree to that too?"

"Sister, I understand, it wasn't Sister Hui who asked me out. Uncle had something to discuss with me. I left the letter he sent in the wastepaper basket downstairs. You can ask A Fu."

"Read this letter before you speak!"

I suspiciously unfolded the crumpled paper. It was my own handwriting, but there were two extra lines of pencil writing under the signature. Looking closely, I recognized:

"Brother, I accept all your advice. I will start over and be a person again. With the love we had when we were little, you can always forgive me. Today, I will use your coming or not coming to predict our result!"

Sister Min glared at me. My crime was judged and decided. No matter what I said, these two lines of pencil writing could not be forgiven.

A willow tree along the street, blown by the wind, peered in. The room was silent, with two people who didn't speak.
